    </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:GU" title="ISO 3166-2:GU">\n          GU\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n title=".gu">\n          .gu\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="line-height:11pt">\n          <b>\n           Website\n          </b>\n          <br/>\n          <a class="external text" href="http://www.guam.gov/" rel="nofollow">\n           guam.gov\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Guam\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xa1/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">\n            \xc9\xa1\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'w\' in \'wind\'">\n            w\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: \'a\' in \'father\'">\n            \xc9\x91\xcb\x90\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">\n            m\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <small class="nowrap">\n         (\n         <span class="unicode haudio">\n          <span class="fn">\n           <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Guam.ogg" title="About this sound">\n             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n            </a>\n           </span>\n           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/30/En-us-Guam.ogg" title="En-us-Guam.ogg">\n            listen\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         )\n        </small>\n       </span>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">\n        Chamorro\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n        <span lang="cha">\n         Gu\xc3\xa5h\xc3\xa5n\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">\n         [\xcb\x88\xc9\xa1\xca\xb7\xc9\x91h\xc9\x91n]\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       ; formerly in\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n        Guaj\xc3\xa1n\n       </i>\n       ) is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">\n        unincorporated and organized territory of the United States\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">\n        Micronesia\n       </a>\n       in the western Pacific Ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oia_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-oia-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The capital city of Guam is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hag%C3%A5t%C3%B1a,_Guam" title="Hag\xc3\xa5t\xc3\xb1a, Guam">\n        Hag\xc3\xa5t\xc3\xb1a\n       </a>\n       and the most populous city is\n       <a href="/wiki/Dededo" title="Dededo">\n        Dededo\n       </a>\n       . The inhabitants of Guam are called Guamanians, and they are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizenship_in_the_United_States" title="Citizenship in the United States">\n        American citizens\n       </a>\n       by birth. Indigenous Guamanians are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">\n        Chamorros\n       </a>\n       , who are related to other\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian" title="Austronesian">\n        Austronesian\n       </a>\n       natives to the west in the Philippines and Taiwan.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2016, 162,742 people resided on Guam. Guam has an area of 210 square miles (540\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) and a population density of 775 per square mile (299/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). In\n       <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">\n        Oceania\n       </a>\n       , it is the largest and southernmost of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">\n        Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       and the largest island in Micronesia. Among its municipalities,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mongmong-Toto-Maite" title="Mongmong-Toto-Maite">\n        Mongmong-Toto-Maite\n       </a>\n       has the highest population density at 3,691 per square mile (1,425/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), whereas\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inarajan,_Guam" title="Inarajan, Guam">\n        Inarajan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umatac,_Guam" title="Umatac, Guam">\n        Umatac\n       </a>\n       have the lowest density at 119 per square mile (46/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). The highest point is\n       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lamlam" title="Mount Lamlam">\n        Mount Lamlam\n       </a>\n       at 1,332 feet (406\xc2\xa0m) above sea level. Since the 1960s,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Guam" title="Economy of Guam">\n        the economy\n       </a>\n       has been supported by two industries: tourism and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">\n        United States Armed Forces\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rogers-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The indigenous\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">\n        Chamorros\n       </a>\n       settled the island approximately 4,000 years ago. Portuguese explorer\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">\n        Ferdinand Magellan\n       </a>\n       , while in the service of Spain, was the first European to visit the island on March 6, 1521. Guam was colonized by Spain in 1668 with settlers, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Luis_de_San_Vitores" title="Diego Luis de San Vitores">\n        Diego Luis de San Vitores\n       </a>\n       , a Catholic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit_missionary" title="Jesuit missionary">\n        Jesuit missionary\n       </a>\n       . Between the 16th century and the 18th century, Guam was an important stopover for the Spanish\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_Galleons" title="Manila Galleons">\n        Manila Galleons\n       </a>\n       . During the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">\n        Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War\n       </a>\n       , the United States\n       <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Guam" title="Capture of Guam">\n        captured Guam\n       </a>\n       on June 21, 1898. Under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">\n        Treaty of Paris\n       </a>\n       , Spain ceded Guam to the United States on December 10, 1898. Guam is among the seventeen\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">\n        non-self-governing territories listed by the United Nations\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Before\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       , there were only five American jurisdictions in the Pacific Ocean, these being, Guam and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">\n        Wake Island\n       </a>\n       in Micronesia,\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">\n        American Samoa\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawai%27i" title="Hawai\'i">\n        Hawai\'i\n       </a>\n       in Polynesia, and the Philippines in the Malay Archipelago of Southeast Asia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On December 7, 1941, hours after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">\n        attack on Pearl Harbor\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guam_(1941)" title="Battle of Guam (1941)">\n        Guam was captured\n       </a>\n       by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">\n        Japanese\n       </a>\n       , who occupied the island for two and a half years. During the occupation, Guamanians were subjected to beheadings, forced labor, rape, and torture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guam_(1944)" title="Battle of Guam (1944)">\n        American forces recaptured the island\n       </a>\n       on July 21, 1944;\n       <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day" title="Liberation Day">\n        Liberation Day\n       </a>\n       commemorates the victory.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An unofficial but frequently used territorial motto is "Where America\'s Day Begins", which refers to the island\'s close proximity to the international date line.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2">\n           <a href="#Magellan.27s_travel_to_Guam">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.1\n            </span>\n            <span href="#Spanish_colonization_and_the_Manila_galleons">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Spanish colonization and the Manila galleons\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">\n           <a href="#Internal_conflicts">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Internal conflicts\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5">\n           <a href="#Expulsion_of_the_Jesuits">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Expulsion of the Jesuits\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6">\n           <a href="#Post-Napoleonic_era">\n <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#Spanish.E2.80.93American_War_and_World_War_II">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War and World War II\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n      </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9">\n           <a href="#Vietnam_War_and_later">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.8\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Vietnam War and later\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a  <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Climate">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Climate\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#Demographics">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Demographics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Ethnic_groups">\n Language\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Religion">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#Sports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21">\n             <a href="#Swimming">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.1.4\n              </span>\n              <span  <span class="toctext">\n               Mixed martial arts\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Government and politics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Political_status">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Political status\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#Villages">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Villages\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#Military_bases">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Military bases\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#Transportation_and_communications">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Transportation and communications\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#Ecology">\n          <span          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35">\n           <a href="#Wildfires">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             11.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Wildfires\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36">\n           <a href="#Aquatic_preserves">\n            <span       </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37">\n         <a href="#Education">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Education\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38">\n           <a href="#Colleges_and_universities">\n            <span    </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">\n         <a href="#Health_care">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Health care\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">\n         <a href="#Film-making">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Film-making\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           16\n          </span>\n class="tocnumber">\n           17\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guam" title="History of Guam">\n        History of Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferdinand_Magellan_(Retouched).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="448" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg/220px-Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg/330px-Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg/440px-Ferdinand_Magellan_%28Retouched%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferdinand_Magellan_(Retouched).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">\n          Ferdinand Magellan\n         </a>\n         , Portuguese navigator who discovered Guam (March 6, 1521) during his circumnavigation of the globe.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The original inhabitants of Guam and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">\n        Northern Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">\n        Chamorro people\n       </a>\n       , who are believed to be descendants of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" title="Austronesian people">\n        Austronesian people\n       </a>\n       originating from Southeast Asia as early as 2000 BC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :16\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The ancient Chamorro society had four classes:\n       <i>\n        chamorri\n       </i>\n       (chiefs),\n       <i>\n        matua\n       </i>\n       (upper class),\n       <i>\n        achaot\n       </i>\n       (middle class), and\n       <i>\n        mana\'chang\n       </i>\n       (lower class).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :20\xe2\x80\x9321\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <i>\n        matua\n       </i>\n       were located in the coastal villages, which meant they had the best access to fishing grounds, whereas the\n       <i>\n        mana\'chang\n       </i>\n       were located in the interior of the island.\n       <i>\n        Matua\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        mana\'chang\n       </i>\n       rarely communicated with each other, and\n       <i>\n        matua\n       </i>\n       often used\n       <i>\n        achaot\n       </i>\n       as intermediaries. There were also "\n       <i>\n        mak\xc3\xa5hna\n       </i>\n       " (similar to shamans), skilled in healing and medicine. Belief in spirits of ancient Chamorros called "\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taotao_mo%27na" title="Taotao mo\'na">\n         Taotao mo\'na\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       " still persists as a remnant of pre-European culture. Their society was organized along\n       <a href="/wiki/Matrilineality" title="Matrilineality">\n        matrilineal\n       </a>\n       clans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :21\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Latte_stone" title="Latte stone">\n        <i>\n         Latte\n        </i>\n        stones\n       </a>\n       are stone pillars that are found only in the Mariana Islands; they are a recent development in Pre-Contact Chamorro society. The latte-stone was used as a foundation on which thatched huts were built.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :26\n       </sup>\n       Latte stones consist of a base shaped from limestone called the\n       <i>\n        haligi\n       </i>\n       and with a capstone, or\n       <i>\n        t\xc3\xa5sa\n       </i>\n       , made either from a large brain coral or limestone, placed on top.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :27\xe2\x80\x9328\n       </sup>\n       A possible source for these stones, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rota_Latte_Stone_Quarry" title="Rota Latte Stone Quarry">\n        Rota Latte Stone Quarry\n       </a>\n       , was discovered in 1925 on\n       <a href="/wiki/Rota_(island)" title="Rota (island)">\n        Rota\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :28\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Magellan\'s_travel_to_Guam">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Magellan.27s_travel_to_Guam">\n        Magellan\'s travel to Guam\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Magellan\'s travel to Guam">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The first European to travel to Guam was Portuguese navigator\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">\n        Ferdinand Magellan\n       </a>\n       , sailing for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">\n        King of Spain\n       </a>\n       , when he sighted the island on March 6, 1521, during his fleet\'s circumnavigation of the globe.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :41\xe2\x80\x9342\n       </sup>\n       When Magellan arrived on Guam, he was greeted by hundreds of small\n       <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">\n        outrigger canoes\n       </a>\n       that appeared to be flying over the water, due to their considerable speed. These outrigger canoes were called\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proas" title="Proas">\n        Proas\n       </a>\n       , and resulted in Magellan naming Guam\n       <i>\n        Islas de las Velas Latinas\n       </i>\n       ("Islands of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lateen_sail" title="Lateen sail">\n        Lateen sails\n       </a>\n       ").\n       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Pigafetta" title="Antonio Pigafetta">\n        Antonio Pigafetta\n       </a>\n       (one of Magellan\'s original 18) said that the name was "Island of Sails", but he also writes that the inhabitants "entered the ships and stole whatever they could lay their hands on", including "the small boat that was fastened to the poop of the flagship."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nowell_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Nowell-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :129\n       </sup>\n       "Those people are poor, but ingenious and very thievish, on account of which we called those three islands\n       <i>\n        Islas de los Ladrones\n       </i>\n       ("Islands of thieves")."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nowell_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Nowell-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :131\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_colonization_and_the_Manila_galleons">\n        Spanish colonization and the Manila galleons\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Spanish colonization and the Manila galleons">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Despite Magellan\'s visit, Guam was not officially claimed by Spain until January 26, 1565, by General\n       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel L\xc3\xb3pez de Legazpi">\n        Miguel L\xc3\xb3pez de Legazpi\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :46\n       </sup>\n       From 1565 to 1815, Guam and the Northern Mariana Islands, the only Spanish outpost in the Pacific Ocean east of the Philippines, was an important resting stop for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_galleons" title="Manila galleons">\n        Manila galleons\n       </a>\n       , a fleet that covered the Pacific trade route between\n       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">\n        Acapulco\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">\n        Manila\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :51\n       </sup>\n       To protect these Pacific fleets, Spain built several defensive structures that still stand today, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Nuestra_Senora_de_la_Soledad" title="Fort Nuestra Senora de la Soledad">\n        Fort Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Soledad\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Umatac" title="Umatac">\n        Umatac\n       </a>\n       . Guam is the biggest single segment of\n       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">\n        Micronesia\n       </a>\n       , the largest islands between the island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">\n        Kyushu\n       </a>\n       (Japan),\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">\n        New Guinea\n       </a>\n       , the Philippines, and the Hawaiian Islands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Spanish colonization commenced on June 15, 1668, with the arrival of\n       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Luis_de_San_Vitores" title="Diego Luis de San Vitores">\n        Diego Luis de San Vitores\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Calungsod" title="Pedro Calungsod">\n        Pedro Calungsod\n       </a>\n       , who established the first Catholic church.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :64\n       </sup>\n       The islands were part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">\n        Spanish East Indies\n       </a>\n       governed from the Philippines, which were in turn part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">\n        Viceroyalty of New Spain\n       </a>\n       based in Mexico City. Other reminders of colonial times include the old Governor\'s Palace in\n       <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Hag%C3%A5t%C3%B1a)" title="Plaza de Espa\xc3\xb1a (Hag\xc3\xa5t\xc3\xb1a)">\n        Plaza de Espa\xc3\xb1a\n       </a>\n       and the Spanish Bridge, both in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hagat%C3%B1a" title="Hagat\xc3\xb1a">\n        Hagat\xc3\xb1a\n       </a>\n       . Guam\'s Cathedral\n       <a href="/wiki/Dulce_Nombre_de_Maria_Cathedral_Basilica" title="Dulce Nombre de Maria Cathedral Basilica">\n        Dulce Nombre de Maria\n       </a>\n       was formally opened on February 2, 1669, as was the Royal College of San Juan de Letran.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :68\n       </sup>\n       Guam, along with the rest of the Mariana and\n       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">\n        Caroline Islands\n       </a>\n       , were treated as part of Spain\'s colony in the Philippines. While the island\'s Chamorro culture has indigenous roots, the cultures of both Guam and the Northern Marianas have many similarities with Spanish culture due to three centuries of Spanish rule.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rogers-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_conflicts">\n        Internal conflicts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Internal conflicts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Intermittent warfare lasting from July 23, 1670, until July 1695, plus the typhoons of 1671 and 1693, and in particular the\n       <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">\n        smallpox\n       </a>\n       epidemic of 1688, reduced the Chamorro population from 50,000 to 10,000 to less than 5,000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :86\n       </sup>\n       Precipitated by the death of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quipuha" title="Quipuha">\n        Quipuha\n       </a>\n       , and the murder of Father San Vitores and Pedro Calungsod by local rebel chief\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matapang" title="Matapang">\n        Matapang\n       </a>\n       , tensions led to a number of conflicts. Captain Juan de Santiago started a campaign to conquer the island, which was continued by the successive commanders of the Spanish forces.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :68\xe2\x80\x9374\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After his arrival in 1674, Captain Damian de Esplana ordered the arrest of rebels who attacked the population of certain towns. Hostilities eventually led to the destruction of villages such as Chochogo, Pepura, Tumon, Sidia-Aty, Sagua, Nagan and Ninca.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :74\xe2\x80\x9375\n       </sup>\n       Starting in June 1676, the first Spanish Governor of Guam, Capt. Francisco de Irrisarri y Vinar, controlled internal affairs more strictly than his predecessors in order to curb tensions. He also ordered the construction of schools, roads and other infrastructure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :75\xe2\x80\x9376\n       </sup>\n       Later, Capt. Jose de Quiroga arrived in 1680 and continued some of the development projects started by his predecessors. He also continued the search for the rebels who had assassinated Father San Vitores, resulting in campaigns against the rebels which were hiding out in some islands, eventually leading to the death of Matapang, Hurao and Aguarin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :77\xe2\x80\x9378\n       </sup>\n       Quiroga brought some natives from the northern islands to Guam, ordering the population to live in a few large villages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :78\xe2\x80\x9379\n       </sup>\n       These included Jinapsan, Umatac, Pago, Agat and Inarajan, where he built a number of churches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :79\n       </sup>\n       By July 1695, Quiroga had completed the conquest of Guam, Rota, Tinian and Aguigan.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :85\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Expulsion_of_the_Jesuits">\n        Expulsion of the Jesuits\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Expulsion of the Jesuits">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On February 26, 1767,\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">\n        Charles III of Spain\n       </a>\n       issued a decree confiscating the property of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">\n        Jesuits\n       </a>\n       and banishing them from Spain and her possessions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :101\n       </sup>\n       As a consequence, the Jesuit fathers on Guam departed on November 2, 1769, on the schooner\n       <i>\n        Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Guadalupe\n       </i>\n       , abandoning their churches, rectories and ranches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :102\xe2\x80\x93103\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The arrival of Governor Don Mariano Tobias, on September 15, 1771, brought agricultural reforms, including making land available to the islanders for cultivation, encouraged the development of cattle raising, imported deer and water buffalo from\n       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">\n        Manila\n       </a>\n       , donkeys and mules from\n       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">\n        Acapulco\n       </a>\n       , established cotton mills and\n       <a href="/wiki/Salt_evaporation_pond" title="Salt evaporation pond">\n        salt pans\n       </a>\n       , free public schools, and the first Guam militia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :107\xe2\x80\x93109\n       </sup>\n       Later, he was transferred to Manila in June 1774.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :113\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Napoleonic_era">\n        Post-Napoleonic era\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-Napoleonic era">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Following the\n       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">\n        Napoleonic Wars\n       </a>\n       , many Spanish colonies in the Western Hemisphere had become independent, shifting the economic dependence of Guam from\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       to the Philippines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :144\n       </sup>\n       Don Francisco Ramon de Villalobos, who became governor in 1831, improved economic conditions including the promotion of rice cultivation and the establishment of a leper hospital.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :148\xe2\x80\x93149\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Kotzebue" title="Otto von Kotzebue">\n        Otto von Kotzebue\n       </a>\n       visited the island in November 1817,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :127\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis_de_Freycinet" title="Louis de Freycinet">\n        Louis de Freycinet\n       </a>\n       in March 1819.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :134\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Jules_Dumont_d%27Urville" title="Jules Dumont d\'Urville">\n        Jules Dumont d\'Urville\n       </a>\n       made two visits, the first in May 1828.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :139\n       </sup>\n       The island became a rest stop for\n       <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">\n        whalers\n       </a>\n       starting in 1823.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :145\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A devastating typhoon struck the island on August 10, 1848, followed by a severe earthquake on January 25, 1849, which resulted in many refugees from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">\n        Caroline Islands\n       </a>\n       , victims of the resultant\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">\n        tsunami\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :151\n       </sup>\n       After a smallpox epidemic killed 3,644 Guamanians in 1856, Carolinians and Japanese were permitted to settle in the Marianas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :157\n       </sup>\n       Guam received nineteen Filipino prisoners after their failed\n       <a href="/wiki/1872_Cavite_mutiny" title="1872 Cavite mutiny">\n        1872 Cavite mutiny\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carano_13-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carano-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :160\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American_War_and_World_War_II">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish.E2.80.93American_War_and_World_War_II">\n        Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War and World War II\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War and World War II">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:205px;max-width:205px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:203px;max-width:203px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Three_Marines_and_their_machine_gun_on_Guam.jpg">\n           <img alt="Three U.S.  Marines and their machine gun lay heavy fire on a Japanese sniper nest (July 28, 1944)." data-file-height="744" data-file-width="942" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Three_Marines_and_their_machine_gun_on_Guam.jpg/201px-Three_Marines_and_their_machine_gun_on_Guam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Three_Marines_and_their_machine_gun_on_Guam.jpg/302px-Three_Marines_and_their_machine_gun_on_Guam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Three_Marines_and_their_machine_gun_on_Guam.jpg/402px-Three_Marines_and_their_machine_gun_on_Guam.jpg 2x" width="201"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">\n           U.S. Marines\n          </a>\n          laying machine gun fire on a Japanese sniper nest during the liberation battle on Guam, (July 28, 1944)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After almost four centuries as part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Spain" title="Kingdom of Spain">\n        Kingdom of Spain\n       </a>\n       and its 400 year old, globe-girdling\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">\n        Spanish Empire\n       </a>\n       , the United States\n       <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Guam" title="Capture of Guam">\n        occupied\n       </a>\n       the island following Spain\'s defeat in the 1898\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">\n        Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War\n       </a>\n       , as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">\n        Treaty of Paris\n       </a>\n       of 1898. Guam was transferred to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">\n        United States Navy\n       </a>\n       control on December 23, 1898, by\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Executive_Order_108-A" title="s:Executive Order 108-A">\n        Executive Order 108-A\n       </a>\n       from 25th President\n       <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">\n        William McKinley\n       </a>\n       . Guam came to serve as a station for American merchant and warships traveling to and from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Philippines" title="The Philippines">\n        the Philippines\n       </a>\n       (another American acquisition from Spain) while the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">\n        Northern Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       were sold by Spain to Germany for part of its rapidly expanding\n       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">\n        German Empire\n       </a>\n       , then following the German defeat in\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">\n        World War I\n       </a>\n       (1914-1918) became a\n       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">\n        League of Nations\n       </a>\n       Mandate in 1919 with the nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">\n        Empire of Japan\n       </a>\n       as the mandatory ("trustee") as a member nation of the victorious\n       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">\n        Allies\n       </a>\n       in the "Great War".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_5-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rogers-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A U.S. Navy yard was established at\n       <a href="/wiki/Piti,_Guam" title="Piti, Guam">\n        Piti\n       </a>\n       in 1899, and a\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">\n        United States Marine Corps\n       </a>\n       barracks at Sumay in 1901.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rottman_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rottman-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :13\n       </sup>\n       Following the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine\xe2\x80\x93American War">\n        Philippine\xe2\x80\x93American War\n       </a>\n       (also known as the Philippine Insurrection, 1899-1902), rebel nationalist leaders\n       <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo" title="Emilio Aguinaldo">\n        Emilio Aguinaldo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Apolinario_Mabini" title="Apolinario Mabini">\n        Apolinario Mabini\n       </a>\n       were exiled on Guam in 1901 after their capture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mabini_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mabini-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :vi\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A marine seaplane unit was stationed in Guam from 1921 to 1930, the first in the Pacific.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rottman_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rottman-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :13\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">\n        Pan American World Airways\n       </a>\n       established a seaplane base on the island for its trans-Pacific San Francisco-Manila-Hong Kong route, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Pacific_Cable_Company" title="Commercial Pacific Cable Company">\n        Commercial Pacific Cable Company\n       </a>\n       had earlier built a telegraph/telephone station in 1903 for its trans-oceanic communication line.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rottman_15-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rottman-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :15\n       </sup>\n       During\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       (1939-1945), Guam was\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guam_(1941)" title="Battle of Guam (1941)">\n        attacked and invaded\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       on Monday, December 8, 1941, shortly after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">\n        attack on Pearl Harbor\n       </a>\n       \'s American Pacific fleet and naval/air bases in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">\n        Hawaii\n       </a>\n       , hours before. In addition, Japan made major military moves into Southeast Asia and the\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">\n        East Indies\n       </a>\n       islands of the South Pacific Ocean against the British and Dutch colonies, opening a new wider Pacific phase in the Second World War.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach,_Guam.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="941" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach%2C_Guam.jpg/220px-US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach%2C_Guam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach%2C_Guam.jpg/330px-US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach%2C_Guam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach%2C_Guam.jpg/440px-US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach%2C_Guam.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Marine_Corps_155mm_rifle_on_White_Beach,_Guam.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Battle of Guam, July 1944\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">\n        Northern Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       had become a League of Nations mandate assigned to Japan in 1919, pursuant to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">\n        Treaty of Versailles\n       </a>\n       of 1919. It was the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chamorros" title="Chamorros">\n        Chamorros\n       </a>\n       indigenous island people from the Northern Marianas who were brought to Guam to serve as interpreters and in other capacities for the occupying Japanese force. The Guamanian Chamorros were treated as an occupied enemy by the Japanese military. After the war, this would cause resentment between the Guamanian Chamorros and the Chamorros of the Northern Marianas. Guam\'s Chamorros believed their northern brethren should have been compassionate towards them, whereas having been administered by Japan for over 30 years, the Northern Mariana Chamorros were loyal to the Japanese government.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Japanese occupation of Guam lasted for approximately thirty-one months. During this period, the indigenous people of Guam were subjected to forced labor, family separation, incarceration, execution, concentration camps and forced prostitution. Approximately one thousand people died during the occupation, according to later\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">\n        Congressional\n       </a>\n       committee testimony in 2004. Some historians estimate that war violence killed 10% of Guam\'s then 20,000 population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The United States returned and fought the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guam_(1944)" title="Battle of Guam (1944)">\n        Battle of Guam\n       </a>\n       from July 21 to August 10, 1944, to recapture the island from Japanese military occupation. More than 18,000 Japanese were killed as only 485 surrendered. Sergeant\n       <a href="/wiki/Shoichi_Yokoi" title="Shoichi Yokoi">\n        Shoichi Yokoi\n       </a>\n       , who surrendered in January 1972, appears to have been the last confirmed\n       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_holdout" title="Japanese holdout">\n        Japanese holdout\n       </a>\n       for 28 years in the forested back country on Guam.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The United States also captured and occupied the nearby Northern Marianas Islands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        North Field\n       </b>\n       was established in 1944, and was renamed for Brigadier General\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Roy_Andersen" title="James Roy Andersen">\n        James Roy Andersen\n       </a>\n       (1904\xe2\x80\x931945) of the old\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">\n        U.S. Army Air Forces\n       </a>\n       as\n       <a href="/wiki/Andersen_Air_Force_Base" title="Andersen Air Force Base">\n        Andersen Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war">\n        Post-war\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-war">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="788" data-file-width="1118" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg/220px-B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg/330px-B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg/440px-B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B-52_Guam_Linebacker_II_-_Copia.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-52_Stratofortress" title="Boeing B-52 Stratofortress">\n          B-52\n         </a>\n         at Andersen Air Force Base, during\n         <a href="/wiki/Operation_Linebacker_II" title="Operation Linebacker II">\n          Operation Linebacker II\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">\n          Vietnam War\n         </a>\n         , 1972\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After World War II, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Organic_Act_of_1950" title="Guam Organic Act of 1950">\n        Guam Organic Act of 1950\n       </a>\n       established Guam as an\n       <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">\n        unincorporated organized territory of the United States\n       </a>\n       , provided for the structure of the island\'s civilian government, and granted the people U.S. citizenship. The Governor of Guam was federally appointed until 1968, when the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guam_Elective_Governor_Act" title="Guam Elective Governor Act">\n        Guam Elective Governor Act\n       </a>\n       provided for the office\'s popular election.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :242\n       </sup>\n       Since Guam is not a U.S. state, U.S. citizens residing on Guam are not allowed to vote for president and their congressional representative is a non-voting member.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_5-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rogers-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They do, however, get to vote for party delegates in presidential primaries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curry_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Curry-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam_War_and_later">\n        Vietnam War and later\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Vietnam War and later">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Arc_Light" title="Operation Arc Light">\n        Operation Arc Light\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Rolling_Thunder" title="Operation Rolling Thunder">\n        Operation Rolling Thunder\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Andersen Air Force Base played a major role in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">\n        Vietnam War\n       </a>\n       . The host unit was later designated the\n       <a href="/wiki/36th_Wing#Pacific_Air_Forces" title="36th Wing">\n        36th Wing\n       </a>\n       (36 WG), assigned to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Air_Forces" title="Pacific Air Forces">\n        Pacific Air Forces\n       </a>\n       (PACAF)\n       <a href="/wiki/Thirteenth_Air_Force" title="Thirteenth Air Force">\n        Thirteenth Air Force\n       </a>\n       (13AF). In September 2012, 13 AF was inactivated and its functions merged into PACAF. The multinational\n       <a href="/wiki/Cope_North" title="Cope North">\n        Cope North\n       </a>\n       military exercise is an annual event.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On August 6, 1997, Guam was the site of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air_Flight_801" title="Korean Air Flight 801">\n        Korean Air Flight 801\n       </a>\n       aircraft accident. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">\n        Boeing 747\xe2\x80\x93300\n       </a>\n       jetliner was preparing to land when it crashed into a hill, killing 228 of the 254 people on board. Since 1974, about\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_Guam" title="National Register of Historic Places listings in Guam">\n        124 historic sites in Guam\n       </a>\n       have been recognized under the U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">\n        National Register of Historic Places\n       </a>\n       . Guam temporarily hosted 100,000 Vietnamese refugees in 1975, and 6,600\n       <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">\n        Kurdish\n       </a>\n       refugees in 1996.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rottman_15-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rottman-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :17\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In August 2017,\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">\n        North Korea\n       </a>\n       warned that it might launch mid-range ballistic missiles into waters within 18 to 24 miles of Guam, following an\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Korea%E2%80%93United_States_relations#Trump_administration" title="North Korea\xe2\x80\x93United States relations">\n        exchange of threats\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnbc-20170810_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cnbc-20170810-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       between the governments of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kim_dynasty_(North_Korea)#Kim_Jong-un" title="Kim dynasty (North Korea)">\n        North Korea\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trump_administration" title="Trump administration">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:583px;max-width:583px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:109px;max-width:109px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guam_ali_2011364_lrg.jpg">\n           <img alt="An unobstructed view of the island of Guam from NASA\'s Earth Observing-1 satellite" data-file-height="6021" data-file-width="4014" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Guam_ali_2011364_lrg.jpg/107px-Guam_ali_2011364_lrg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Guam_ali_2011364_lrg.jpg/161px-Guam_ali_2011364_lrg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Guam_ali_2011364_lrg.jpg/214px-Guam_ali_2011364_lrg.jpg 2x" width="107"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Guam from satellite\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:226px;max-width:226px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_030225-N-0000X-002_An_aerial_view_of_Apra_Harbor_on_U.S._Naval_Base_Guam_is_seen_during_a_fly-by,_Feb._25,_2003.jpg">\n           <img alt="Aerial view of Apra Harbor" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/US_Navy_030225-N-0000X-002_An_aerial_view_of_Apra_Harbor_on_U.S._Naval_Base_Guam_is_seen_during_a_fly-by%2C_Feb._25%2C_2003.jpg/224px-US_Navy_030225-N-0000X-002_An_aerial_view_of_Apra_Harbor_on_U.S._Naval_Base_Guam_is_seen_during_a_fly-by%2C_Feb._25%2C_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/US_Navy_030225-N-0000X-002_An_aerial_view_of_Apra_Harbor_on_U.S._Naval_Base_Guam_is_seen_during_a_fly-by%2C_Feb._25%2C_2003.jpg/336px-US_Navy_030225-N-0000X-002_An_aerial_view_of_Apra_Harbor_on_U.S._Naval_Base_Guam_is_seen_during_a_fly-by%2C_Feb._25%2C_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/US_Navy_030225-N-0000X-002_An_aerial_view_of_Apra_Harbor_on_U.S._Naval_Base_Guam_is_seen_during_a_fly-by%2C_Feb._25%2C_2003.jpg/448px-US_Navy_030225-N-0000X-002_An_aerial_view_of_Apra_Harbor_on_U.S._Naval_Base_Guam_is_seen_during_a_fly-by%2C_Feb._25%2C_2003.jpg 2x" width="224"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Aerial view of\n          <a href="/wiki/Apra_Harbor" title="Apra Harbor">\n           Apra Harbor\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:242px;max-width:242px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_on_Guam.jpg">\n           <img alt="Sunset on Guam" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Sunset_on_Guam.jpg/240px-Sunset_on_Guam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Sunset_on_Guam.jpg/360px-Sunset_on_Guam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Sunset_on_Guam.jpg/480px-Sunset_on_Guam.jpg 2x" width="240"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Sunset on Guam\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Guam" title="Geography of Guam">\n        Geography of Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Guam lies between 13.2\xc2\xb0N and 13.7\xc2\xb0N and between 144.6\xc2\xb0E and 145.0\xc2\xb0E, and has an area of 212 square miles (549\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), making it the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_United_States_by_area" title="List of islands of the United States by area">\n        32nd largest island of the United States\n       </a>\n       . It is the southernmost and largest island in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marianas" title="Marianas">\n        Mariana\n       </a>\n       island chain and is also the largest island in\n       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">\n        Micronesia\n       </a>\n       . This island chain was created by the colliding Pacific and Philippine Sea tectonic plates. Guam is the closest land mass to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">\n        Mariana Trench\n       </a>\n       , a deep\n       <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">\n        subduction zone\n       </a>\n       , that lies beside the island chain to the east.\n       <a href="/wiki/Challenger_Deep" title="Challenger Deep">\n        Challenger Deep\n       </a>\n       , the deepest surveyed point in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oceans" title="Oceans">\n        Oceans\n       </a>\n       , is southwest of Guam at 35,797 feet (10,911 meters) deep. The highest point in Guam is\n       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lamlam" title="Mount Lamlam">\n        Mount Lamlam\n       </a>\n       at an elevation of 1,334 feet (407 meters).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guam_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Guam-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The island of Guam is 30 miles (50\xc2\xa0km) long and 4 to 12 miles (6 to 19\xc2\xa0km) wide, three-fourths the size of\n       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">\n        Singapore\n       </a>\n       . The island experiences occasional earthquakes due to its location on the western edge of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">\n        Pacific Plate\n       </a>\n       and near the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea_Plate" title="Philippine Sea Plate">\n        Philippine Sea Plate\n       </a>\n       . In recent years, earthquakes with epicenters near Guam have had magnitudes ranging from 5.0 to 8.7. Unlike the\n       <a href="/wiki/Anatahan" title="Anatahan">\n        Anatahan\n       </a>\n       volcano in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">\n        Northern Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       , Guam is not volcanically active. However, due to its proximity to Anatahan,\n       <a href="/wiki/Vog" title="Vog">\n        vog\n       </a>\n       (i.e. volcanic smog) does occasionally affect Guam.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_Anahatan_Volcano_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USGS_Anahatan_Volcano-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A coral table reef surrounds most of Guam, and the limestone plateau provides the source for most of the island\'s fresh water. Steep coastal cliffs dominate the north, while the southern end of the island is mountainous, with lower hills in between.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_1-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Guam experiences a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">\n        tropical rainforest climate\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Af\n       </i>\n       ) \xe2\x80\x93 though its driest month of March almost averages dry enough to qualify as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">\n        tropical monsoon climate\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 moderated by seasonal easterly\n       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">\n        trade winds\n       </a>\n       . The weather is generally very warm with little seasonal temperature variation. The mean high temperature is 86\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F or 30\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C and mean low is 76\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (24.4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) with an average annual rainfall between 1981 and 2010 of around 98 inches or 2,490 millimetres. Temperatures rarely exceed 90\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (32.2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) or fall below 70\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (21.1\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). The relative humidity commonly exceeds 84 percent at night throughout the year, but the average monthly humidity hovers near 66 percent. The dry season runs from December to June. The remaining months (July to November) constitute the wet season. The months of January and February are considered the coolest months of the year with overnight low temperatures of 70 to 75\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (21.1 to 23.9\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) and generally less oppressive humidity levels. The highest temperature ever recorded in Guam was 96\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (35.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on April 18, 1971, and April 1, 1990, and the lowest temperature ever recorded was 65\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (18.3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on February 8, 1973.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guam is located in\n       <i>\n        Typhoon Alley\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and it is common for the island to be threatened by tropical storms and possible\n       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">\n        typhoons\n       </a>\n       during the wet season. The highest risk of typhoons is during August through October. They can, however, occur year-round. The most intense typhoon to pass over Guam recently was\n       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Pongsona" title="Typhoon Pongsona">\n        Super Typhoon Pongsona\n       </a>\n       , with sustained winds of 144 miles per hour (232\xc2\xa0km/h), gusts to 173 miles per hour (278\xc2\xa0km/h), which slammed Guam on December 8, 2002, leaving massive destruction. The wettest month on recruit at Guam Airport has been August 1997 with 38.49 inches (977.6\xc2\xa0mm) and the driest February 2015 with 0.15 inches (3.8\xc2\xa0mm). The wettest calendar year has been 1976 with 131.70 inches (3,345.2\xc2\xa0mm) and the driest 1998 with 57.88 inches (1,470.2\xc2\xa0mm). The most rainfall in a single day occurred on 15 October 1953 when 15.48 inches or 393.2 millimetres fell.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since\n       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Pamela_(1976)" title="Typhoon Pamela (1976)">\n        Super Typhoon Pamela\n       </a>\n       in 1976, wooden structures have been largely replaced by concrete structures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the 1980s wooden utility poles began to be replaced by typhoon-resistant concrete and steel poles. After the local Government enforced stricter construction codes, many home and business owners built their structures out of reinforced concrete with installed\n       <a class="mw-redirect"
