people">\n          Chamorro people\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">\n        Ethnic groups\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Based on a 2010 estimate, the largest ethnic group are the native\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">\n        Chamorros\n       </a>\n       , accounting for 37.3% of the total population. Other significant ethnic groups include those of\n       <a href="/wiki/Filipinos" title="Filipinos">\n        Filipino\n       </a>\n       (26.3%),\n       <a href="/wiki/White_Americans" title="White Americans">\n        White\n       </a>\n       (7.1%), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chuukese_people" title="Chuukese people">\n        Chuukese\n       </a>\n       (7%) ethnicities. The rest are from other Pacific Islands or of\n       <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">\n        Asian\n       </a>\n       ancestry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_1-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">\n        Language\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Language">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The official languages of the island are English and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">\n        Chamorro\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">\n        Religion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">\n        Pew Research Center\n       </a>\n       , 2010:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">\n         Roman Catholic\n        </a>\n        75%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">\n         Protestants\n        </a>\n        17.7%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Unaffiliated 1.7%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Other religions 1.6%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Folk religions 1.5%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Other Christians 1.4%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">\n         Buddhists\n        </a>\n        1.1%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox">\n         Eastern Orthodox\n        </a>\n        &lt;1%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">\n         Hindu\n        </a>\n        &lt;1%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">\n         Muslim\n        </a>\n        &lt;1%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">\n         Jews\n        </a>\n        &lt;1%\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">\n        Culture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          This section\n          <b>\n           does not\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">\n            cite\n           </a>\n           any\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            sources\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please help\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit">\n            improve this section\n           </a>\n           by\n           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">\n            adding citations to reliable sources\n           </a>\n           . Unsourced material may be challenged and\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            removed\n           </a>\n           .\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (July 2017)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guam" title="Music of Guam">\n        Music of Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Guam" title="Culture of Guam">\n        Culture of Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Post-European-contact\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">\n        Chamorro\n       </a>\n       Guamanian culture is a combination of American, Spanish, Filipino, other Micronesian Islander and Mexican traditions. Few indigenous pre-Hispanic customs remained following Spanish contact. Hispanic influences are manifested in the local language, music, dance, sea navigation, cuisine, fishing, games (such as batu, chonka, estuleks, and bayogu), songs and fashion.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During Spanish colonial rule (1668\xe2\x80\x931898) the majority of the population was converted to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">\n        Roman Catholicism\n       </a>\n       and religious festivities such as Easter and Christmas became widespread. Post-contact Chamorro cuisine is largely based on corn, and includes tortillas, tamales, atole and chilaquiles, which are a clear influence from\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">\n        Mesoamerica\n       </a>\n       , principally Mexico, from Spanish trade with Asia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The modern\n       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">\n        Chamorro language\n       </a>\n       has many historical parallels to modern\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_languages" title="Philippine languages">\n        Philippine languages\n       </a>\n       in that it is an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_language" title="Austronesian language">\n        Austronesian language\n       </a>\n       which has absorbed much Spanish vocabulary. It is a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian_language" title="Malayo-Polynesian language">\n        Malayo-Polynesian language\n       </a>\n       , along with such languages as Tagalog, Indonesian, Hawaiian, and even Maori. Despite being spoken in the mid Pacific Ocean, which is geographically closer to speakers of the Polynesian Islands, Chamorro is actually an outlier of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sunda%E2%80%93Sulawesi_languages" title="Sunda\xe2\x80\x93Sulawesi languages">\n        Sunda\xe2\x80\x93Sulawesi languages\n       </a>\n       subgroup. Chamorro is thus more closely related to, and a part of, the languages of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">\n        Malay Archipelago\n       </a>\n       , rather than its neighbours in Polynesia. Among the languages of Malay Archipelago, Chamorro is most closely related to the languages in the south of the chain of islands, within Indonesia, rather than the languages of the north, in the Philippines, with which it shares linguistic Spanish colonial influence.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Also like Filipinos, many Chamorros possess\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_name" title="Spanish name">\n        Spanish surnames\n       </a>\n       despite few of the inhabitants actually descending from the Spanish colonisers. Spanish names and surnames were adopted after their conversion to Roman Catholic Christianity in a phenomenon prompted by the imposition of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cat%C3%A1logo_alfab%C3%A9tico_de_apellidos" title="Cat\xc3\xa1logo alfab\xc3\xa9tico de apellidos">\n        Cat\xc3\xa1logo alfab\xc3\xa9tico de apellidos\n       </a>\n       in Guam and other territories of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">\n        Spanish East Indies\n       </a>\n       , most notably the Philippines.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Due to foreign cultural influence from Spain, most aspects of the early indigenous culture have been lost, though there has been a resurgence in preserving any remaining pre-Hispanic culture in the last few decades. Some scholars have traveled throughout the Pacific Islands conducting research to study what the original Chamorro cultural practices such as dance, language, and canoe building may have been like.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puntan_Dos_Amantes_(Guam)_-_DSC01150.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG/220px-Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG/330px-Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG/440px-Puntan_Dos_Amantes_%28Guam%29_-_DSC01150.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puntan_Dos_Amantes_(Guam)_-_DSC01150.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Puntan Dos Amantes\n         </i>\n         ("Two Lovers Point"), a\n         <a href="/wiki/National_Natural_Landmark" title="National Natural Landmark">\n          National Natural Landmark\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPS_PdA_33-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NPS_PdA-33">\n           [33]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         well known for its romantic associations\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Two aspects of indigenous pre-Hispanic culture that withstood time are chenchule\' and inafa\'maolek. Chenchule\' is the intricate system of reciprocity at the heart of Chamorro society. It is rooted in the core value of inafa\'maolek. Historian Lawrence Cunningham in 1992 wrote, "In a Chamorro sense, the land and its produce belong to everyone.\n       <span lang="cha">\n        <a href="/wiki/Inafa%27maolek" title="Inafa\'maolek">\n         Inafa\'maolek\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       , or interdependence, is the key, or central value, in Chamorro culture\xc2\xa0...\n       <span lang="cha">\n        Inafa\'maolek\n       </span>\n       depends on a spirit of cooperation and sharing. This is the armature, or core, that everything in Chamorro culture revolves around. It is a powerful concern for mutuality rather than\n       <a href="/wiki/Individualism" title="Individualism">\n        individualism\n       </a>\n       and private property rights."\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The core culture or Pengngan Chamorro is based on complex social protocol centered upon respect: From sniffing over the hands of the elders (called mangnginge in Chamorro), the passing down of legends, chants, and courtship rituals, to a person asking for permission from spiritual ancestors before entering a jungle or ancient battle grounds. Other practices predating Spanish conquest include\n       <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">\n        galaide\'\n       </a>\n       canoe-making, making of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Belembaotuyan" title="Belembaotuyan">\n        belembaotuyan\n       </a>\n       (a string musical instrument made from a gourd), fashioning of\n       <i>\n        <span lang="cha">\n         \xc3\xa5cho\' atupat\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       slings and slingstones, tool manufacture,\n       <span lang="cha">\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=M%C3%A5tan_Guma%27&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="M\xc3\xa5tan Guma\' (page does not exist)">\n         M\xc3\xa5tan Guma\'\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       burial rituals, and preparation of herbal medicines by\n       <a href="/wiki/Suruhanu" title="Suruhanu">\n        Suruhanu\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Master craftsmen and women specialize in weavings, including plaited work (\n       <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">\n        niyok\n       </a>\n       - and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pandanus" title="Pandanus">\n        \xc3\xa5kgak\n       </a>\n       -leaf baskets, mats, bags, hats, and food containments), loom-woven material (\n       <a href="/wiki/Plumeria" title="Plumeria">\n        kalachucha-hibiscus\n       </a>\n       and banana fiber skirts, belts and burial shrouds), and body ornamentation (bead and shell necklaces, bracelets, earrings, belts and combs made from tortoise shells and\n       <a href="/wiki/Spondylus" title="Spondylus">\n        Spondylus\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The cosmopolitan and multicultural nature of modern Guam poses challenges for Chamorros struggling to preserve their culture and identity amidst forces of acculturation. The increasing numbers of Chamorros, especially Chamorro youth, relocating to the U.S. Mainland has further complicated both definition and preservation of Chamorro identity.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       While only a few masters exist to continue traditional art forms, the resurgence of interest among the Chamorros to preserve the language and culture has resulted in a growing number of young Chamorros who seek to continue the ancient ways of the Chamorro people.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sports">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_Games">\n        Pacific Games\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Pacific Games">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Guam hosted the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Games" title="Pacific Games">\n        Pacific Games\n       </a>\n       in 1975 and 1999. At the\n       <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_Games" title="2007 Pacific Games">\n        2007 Games\n       </a>\n       , Guam finished 7th of 22 countries and 14th at the\n       <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_Games" title="2011 Pacific Games">\n        2011 Games\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soccer">\n        Soccer\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Soccer">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_football_team" title="Guam national football team">\n        Guam national football team\n       </a>\n       was founded in 1975 and joined\n       <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">\n        FIFA\n       </a>\n       in 1996.\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_football_team" title="Guam national football team">\n        Guam\n       </a>\n       was once considered one of FIFA\'s weakest teams, and experienced their first victory over a FIFA-registered side in 2009, when they defeated\n       <a href="/wiki/Mongolia_national_football_team" title="Mongolia national football team">\n        Mongolia\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Asian_Cup" title="East Asian Cup">\n        East Asian Cup\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guam entered the\n       <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">\n        2018 FIFA World Cup qualification\n       </a>\n       Group D. Guam hosted qualifying games on the island for the first time in 2015. During the qualifying round, Guam clinched their first FIFA World Cup Qualifying win by defeating\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_national_football_team" title="Turkmenistan national football team">\n        Turkmenistan\n       </a>\n       . Since then, the team has experienced moderate success in the Qualifying Round with a record of 2\xe2\x80\x931\xe2\x80\x931.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The national team plays at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_National_Football_Stadium" title="Guam National Football Stadium">\n        Guam National Football Stadium\n       </a>\n       , which has a capacity of 1,000. The men\'s national football team are known as the "matao" team. Matao is the definition of highest level or "noble" class; the matao team have done exceptionally well under the head coach Gary White. As of 2016, the Matao is led by\n       <a href="/wiki/Darren_Sawatzky" title="Darren Sawatzky">\n        Darren Sawatzky\n       </a>\n       , the current head coach.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The top football division in Guam is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guam_Men%27s_Soccer_League" title="Guam Men\'s Soccer League">\n        Guam Men\'s Soccer League\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Rovers_FC_(Guam)" title="Rovers FC (Guam)">\n        Rovers FC\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Shipyard" title="Guam Shipyard">\n        Guam Shipyard\n       </a>\n       are the league\'s most competitive and successful clubs, both have won nine championships in the past years.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">\n        Basketball\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Basketball">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_basketball_team" title="Guam national basketball team">\n        Guam national basketball team\n       </a>\n       is traditionally one of the top teams in the\n       <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Oceania" title="FIBA Oceania">\n        Oceania region\n       </a>\n       behind\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Australia men\'s national basketball team">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_basketball_team" title="New Zealand national basketball team">\n        New Zealand\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2015, it is the reigning champion of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Games_Basketball_Tournament" title="Pacific Games Basketball Tournament">\n        Pacific Games Basketball Tournament\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guam is home to various basketball organizations, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Basketball_Association" title="Guam Basketball Association">\n        GBA\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Swimming">\n        Swimming\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Swimming">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">\n        2012 Summer Olympics\n       </a>\n       in London,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pilar_Shimizu" title="Pilar Shimizu">\n        Pilar Shimizu\n       </a>\n       competed for Guam and placed 42nd in the breaststroke competition.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_union">\n        Rugby union\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Rugby union">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Guam is represented in\n       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">\n        rugby union\n       </a>\n       by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_national_rugby_union_team" title="Guam national rugby union team">\n        Guam national rugby union team\n       </a>\n       . The team has never qualified for a\n       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup" title="Rugby World Cup">\n        Rugby World Cup\n       </a>\n       . Guam played their first match in 2005, an 8\xe2\x80\x938 draw with\n       <a href="/wiki/India_national_rugby_union_team" title="India national rugby union team">\n        India\n       </a>\n       . Guam\'s biggest win was a 74\xe2\x80\x930 defeat of\n       <a href="/wiki/Brunei_national_rugby_union_team" title="Brunei national rugby union team">\n        Brunei\n       </a>\n       in June 2008.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mixed_martial_arts">\n        Mixed martial arts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mixed martial arts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UFC" title="UFC">\n        UFC\n       </a>\n       fighter\n       <a href="/wiki/Jon_Tuck" title="Jon Tuck">\n        Jon Tuck\n       </a>\n       , who boasts a professional record of 10 wins and 4 losses, three of those wins while with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UFC" title="UFC">\n        UFC\n       </a>\n       , fights out of Guam.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009_GU_Proof.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1081" data-file-width="1078" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2009_GU_Proof.png/170px-2009_GU_Proof.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2009_GU_Proof.png/255px-2009_GU_Proof.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/2009_GU_Proof.png/340px-2009_GU_Proof.png 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009_GU_Proof.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         2009 Guam\n         <a href="/wiki/Quarter_(United_States_coin)" title="Quarter (United States coin)">\n          quarter\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Guam" title="Energy in Guam">\n        Energy in Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Guam\'s economy depends primarily on tourism, Department of Defense installations and locally owned businesses. Despite paying no income or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Excise_tax" title="Excise tax">\n        excise tax\n       </a>\n       , it receives large transfer payments from the general revenues of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Department of the Treasury">\n        U.S. federal treasury\n       </a>\n       . Under the provisions of a special law by\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">\n        Congress\n       </a>\n       , it is Guam\'s treasury rather than the U.S. treasury that receives the federal income taxes paid by local taxpayers (including military and civilian federal employees assigned to Guam).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Lying in the western Pacific, Guam is a popular destination for Japanese tourists. Its tourist hub,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tumon" title="Tumon">\n        Tumon\n       </a>\n       , features over 20 large hotels, a Duty Free Shoppers Galleria, Pleasure Island district, indoor aquarium, Sandcastle\n       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">\n        Las Vegas\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93styled shows and other shopping and entertainment venues. It is a relatively short flight from Asia or Australia compared to Hawaii, with hotels and seven public golf courses accommodating over a million tourists per year. Although 75% of the tourists are Japanese, Guam receives a sizable number of tourists from South Korea, the U.S., the Philippines, and Taiwan.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Significant sources of revenue include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duty-free" title="Duty-free">\n        duty-free\n       </a>\n       designer shopping outlets, and the American-style malls:\n       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia_Mall" title="Micronesia Mall">\n        Micronesia Mall\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Premier_Outlets" title="Guam Premier Outlets">\n        Guam Premier Outlets\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Agana_Shopping_Center" title="Agana Shopping Center">\n        Agana Shopping Center\n       </a>\n       , and the world\'s largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">\n        Kmart\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg/220px-GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg/330px-GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg/440px-GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GuamAntonioWonPatAirport.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Terminal at\n         <a href="/wiki/Antonio_B._Won_Pat_International_Airport" title="Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport">\n          Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport\n         </a>\n         . The airport hosts a hub of\n         <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">\n          United Airlines\n         </a>\n         , Guam\'s largest private-sector employer.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The economy had been stable since 2000 due to increased tourism. It is expected to stabilize with the transfer of U.S. Marine Corps\'\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3rd_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="3rd Marine Expeditionary Force">\n        3rd Marine Expeditionary Force\n       </a>\n       , currently in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">\n        Okinawa\n       </a>\n       , Japan, (approximately 8,000 Marines, along with their 10,000 dependents), to Guam between 2010 and 2015. In 2003, Guam had a 14% unemployment rate, and the government suffered a $314\xc2\xa0million shortfall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association" title="Compact of Free Association">\n        Compacts of Free Association\n       </a>\n       between the United States, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">\n        Federated States of Micronesia\n       </a>\n       , the Republic of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">\n        Marshall Islands\n       </a>\n       and the Republic of\n       <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">\n        Palau\n       </a>\n       accorded the former entities of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">\n        Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands\n       </a>\n       a political status of "free association" with the United States. The Compacts give citizens of these island nations generally no restrictions to reside in the United States (also its territories), and many were attracted to Guam due to its proximity, environmental, and cultural familiarity. Over the years, it was claimed by some in Guam that the territory has had to bear the brunt of this agreement in the form of public assistance programs and public education for those from the regions involved, and the federal government should compensate the states and territories affected by this type of migration.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Over the years, Congress had appropriated "Compact Impact" aids to Guam, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">\n        Northern Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       and Hawaii, and eventually this appropriation was written into each renewed Compact. Some, however, continue to claim the compensation is not enough or that the distribution of actual compensation received is significantly disproportionate.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Guam\'s largest single private sector employer, with about 1,400 jobs, was\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Micronesia" title="Continental Micronesia">\n        Continental Micronesia\n       </a>\n       , a subsidiary of\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">\n        Continental Airlines\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       it is now a part of\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">\n        United Airlines\n       </a>\n       , a subsidiary of Chicago-based United Continental Holdings, Inc.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the Continental Micronesia annual payroll in Guam was $90 million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blairbright_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Blairbright-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">\n        Government and politics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Government and politics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guam" title="Politics of Guam">\n        Politics of Guam\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Voting_in_Guam" title="Voting in Guam">\n        Voting in Guam\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Guam" title="Political party strength in Guam">\n        Political party strength in Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="217" data-file-width="300" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg/220px-War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/War_in_the_Pacific_National_Historical_Park" title="War in the Pacific National Historical Park">\n          War in the Pacific National Historical Park\n         </a>\n         at\n         <a href="/wiki/Asan,_Guam" title="Asan, Guam">\n          Asan\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Guam is governed by a popularly elected governor and a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">\n        unicameral\n       </a>\n       15-member\n       <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_Guam" title="Legislature of Guam">\n        legislature\n       </a>\n       , whose members are known as senators. Its judiciary is overseen by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Guam" title="Supreme Court of Guam">\n        Supreme Court of Guam\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/District_Court_of_Guam" title="District Court of Guam">\n        District Court of Guam\n       </a>\n       is the court of United States federal jurisdiction in the territory. Guam elects one\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delegate_(United_States_Congress)" title="Delegate (United States Congress)">\n        delegate to the United States House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       , currently Democrat\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madeleine_Z._Bordallo" title="Madeleine Z. Bordallo">\n        Madeleine Z. Bordallo\n       </a>\n       . The delegate does not have a vote on the final passage of legislation, but is accorded a vote in committee, and the privilege to speak to the House. U.S. citizens in Guam vote in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Straw_poll" title="Straw poll">\n        straw poll\n       </a>\n       for their choice in the U.S. Presidential general election, but since Guam has no votes in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College" title="United States Electoral College">\n        Electoral College\n       </a>\n       , the poll has no real effect. However, in sending delegates to the Republican and Democratic national conventions, Guam does have influence in the national presidential race. These delegates are elected by local party\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_primary#Types_of_primaries_and_caucuses" title="United States presidential primary">\n        conventions\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_5-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rogers-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_status">\n        Political status\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Political status">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In the 1980s and early 1990s, there was a significant movement in favor of this U.S. territory becoming a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(United_States_insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (United States insular area)">\n        commonwealth\n       </a>\n       , which would give it a level of self-government similar to\n       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">\n        Puerto Rico\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">\n        Northern Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       . However, the federal government rejected the version of a commonwealth that the government of Guam proposed, because its clauses were incompatible with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_Clause" title="Territorial Clause">\n        Territorial Clause\n       </a>\n       (Art. IV, Sec. 3, cl. 2) of the U.S. Constitution. Other movements advocate U.S. statehood for Guam, union with the state of Hawaii, or union with the Northern Mariana Islands as a single territory, or independence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In a 1982 plebiscite, voters indicated interest in seeking commonwealth status.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The island has been considering another non-binding plebiscite on decolonization since 1998. Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Baza_Calvo" title="Eddie Baza Calvo">\n        Eddie Baza Calvo\n       </a>\n       intended to include one during the island\'s November 2016 elections but it was delayed again.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raymundo_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Raymundo-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3036" data-file-width="2339" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg/160px-Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg/240px-Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg/320px-Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg 2x" width="160"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Governor_Eddie_Calvo.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Baza_Calvo" title="Eddie Baza Calvo">\n          Eddie Baza Calvo\n         </a>\n         , Governor of Guam\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A Commission on Decolonization was established in 1997 to educate the people of Guam about the various political status options in its relationship with the U.S.: statehood, free association and independence. The group was dormant for some years. In 2013, the Commission began seeking funding to start a public education campaign. There were few subsequent developments until late 2016. In early December 2016, the Commission scheduled a series of education sessions in various villages about the current status of Guam\'s relationship with the U.S. and the self-determination options that might be considered.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raymundo_43-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Raymundo-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Commission\'s current Executive Director is Edward Alvarez and there are ten members. The group is also expected to release position papers on independence and statehood but the contents have not yet been completed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">\n        United Nations\n       </a>\n       is in favor of greater self-determination for Guam and other such territories. The UN\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Special_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="Special Committee on Decolonization">\n        Special Committee on Decolonization\n       </a>\n       has agreed to endorse the Governor\'s education plan. The commission\'s May 2016 report states: "With academics from the University of Guam, [the Commission] was working to create and approve educational materials. The Office of the Governor was collaborating closely with the Commission" in developing educational materials for the public.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The United States\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Interior" title="Department of the Interior">\n        Department of the Interior\n       </a>\n       had approved a $300,000 grant for decolonization education, Edward Alvarez told the United Nations Pacific Regional Seminar in May 2016. "We are hopeful that this might indicate a shift in [United States] policy to its Non-Self-Governing Territories such as Guam, where they will be more willing to engage in discussions about our future and offer true support to help push us towards true self-governances and self-determination."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Villages">\n        Villages\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Villages">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Villages_of_Guam" title="Villages of Guam">\n        Villages of Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Guam is divided into nineteen municipalities called villages:\n      </p>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">\n       <ul>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" Agat\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Asan,_Guam" title="Asan, Guam">\n          Asan\xe2\x80\x91Maina\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a   </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merizo,_Guam" title="Merizo, Guam">\n          Merizo\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a        </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinajana,_Guam" title="Sinajana, Guam">\n          Sinajana\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n
