</a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yigo,_Guam" title="Yigo, Guam">\n          Yigo\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Yona,_Guam" title="Yona, Guam">\n          Yona\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military_bases">\n        Military bases\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Military bases">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_(CVN_76)_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg/220px-US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg/330px-US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg/440px-US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_%28CVN_76%29_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_110821-N-AZ907-015_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Ronald_Reagan_(CVN_76)_enters_Apra_Harbor_for_a_scheduled_port_visit.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The aircraft carrier USS\n         <i>\n          Ronald Reagan\n         </i>\n         (CVN 76) enters\n         <a href="/wiki/Apra_Harbor" title="Apra Harbor">\n          Apra Harbor\n         </a>\n         for a scheduled port visit.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         Note:\n         <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Agana" title="Naval Air Station Agana">\n          Naval Air Station Agana\n         </a>\n         has been deactivated.\n        </i>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n         <a href="#cite_note-47">\n          [47]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._military" title="U.S. military">\n        U.S. military\n       </a>\n       maintains jurisdiction over its bases, which cover approximately 39,000 acres (16,000\xc2\xa0ha), or 29% of the island\'s total land area:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        U.S.\n        <a href="/wiki/Naval_Base_Guam" title="Naval Base Guam">\n         Naval Base Guam\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">\n         U.S. Navy\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 Sumay\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        U.S. Coast Guard Sector Guam, \xe2\x80\x93 Sumay\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Andersen_Air_Force_Base" title="Andersen Air Force Base">\n         Andersen Air Force Base\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" title="U.S. Air Force">\n         U.S. Air Force\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93\n        <a href="/wiki/Yigo" title="Yigo">\n         Yigo\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Apra_Harbor" title="Apra Harbor">\n         Apra Harbor\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 Orote peninsula\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Annex" title="Ordnance Annex">\n         Ordnance Annex\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">\n         U.S. Navy\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 South Central Highlands (formerly known as Naval Magazine)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Naval Computer and Telecommunications Station,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">\n         U.S. Navy\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93\n        <a href="/wiki/Barrigada" title="Barrigada">\n         Barrigada\n        </a>\n        and Finegayan\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Joint Force Headquarters-Guam,\n        <a href="/wiki/Guam_National_Guard" title="Guam National Guard">\n         Guam National Guard\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 Radio Barrigada and Fort Juan Muna\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       In addition to on-shore military installations, Guam, along with the rest of the Mariana Islands, is being prepared to be the westernmost military training range for the U.S. Guam is currently viewed as a key military hub that will further allow U.S. military power to be projected via sea and sky.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The U.S. military has proposed building a new aircraft carrier berth on Guam and moving 8,600 Marines, and 9,000 of their dependents, to Guam from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okinawa" title="Okinawa">\n        Okinawa\n       </a>\n       , Japan. Including the required construction workers, this buildup would increase Guam\'s population by 45%. In a February 2010 letter, the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">\n        United States Environmental Protection Agency\n       </a>\n       sharply criticized these plans because of a water shortfall, sewage problems and the impact on coral reefs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By 2012, these plans had been cut to have only a maximum of 4,800 Marines stationed on the island, two thirds of whom would be there on a rotational basis without their dependents.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With the proposed increased military presence stemming from the upcoming preparation efforts and relocation efforts of U.S. Marines from Okinawa, Japan to Guam slated to begin in 2010 and last for the next several years thereafter, the amount of total land that the military will control or tenant may grow to or surpass 40% of the entire landmass of Guam.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In January 2011, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ike_Skelton_National_Defense_Authorization_Act_for_Fiscal_Year_2011" title="Ike Skelton National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2011">\n        Ike Skelton National Defense Authorization Act for FY2011\n       </a>\n       indicated that recent significant events will delay the deadline for realigning U.S. Marine Corps service members and their families from Okinawa to Guam. The transfer may be as late as 2020. In addition, the Defense Authorization Act cut approximately $320 million from the 2011 budget request.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Villagers and the military community are interconnected in many ways. Many villagers serve in the military or are retired. Many active duty personnel and Defense Department civilians also live in the villages outside of the military installation areas. The military and village communities have "adoption" programs where Guam\'s population and military personnel stationed on Guam perform community service projects.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_and_communications">\n        Transportation and communications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transportation and communications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Guam" title="Communications in Guam">\n        Communications in Guam\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Guam" title="Transportation in Guam">\n        Transportation in Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guam_route_marker_8.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1716" data-file-width="1047" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Guam_route_marker_8.svg/130px-Guam_route_marker_8.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Guam_route_marker_8.svg/195px-Guam_route_marker_8.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Guam_route_marker_8.svg/260px-Guam_route_marker_8.svg.png 2x" width="130"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guam_route_marker_8.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Guam Highway 8 route marker\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Most of the island has state-of-the-art mobile phone services and high-speed internet widely available through either cable or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DSL" title="DSL">\n        DSL\n       </a>\n       . Guam was added to the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">\n        North American Numbering Plan (NANP)\n       </a>\n       in 1997 (country code 671 became NANP\n       <a href="/wiki/Area_code_671" title="Area code 671">\n        area code 671\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       removing the barrier of high-cost international long-distance calls to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">\n        U.S. mainland\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guam is also a major hub for submarine cables between the Western U.S., Hawaii, Australia and Asia. Guam currently serves twelve submarine cables, with most continuing to China.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="1547" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg/220px-US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg/330px-US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg/440px-US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_to_Guam_First_Flight_Cover_1935.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cover carried both directions on the first commercial flights between Guam and the United States, October 5\xe2\x80\x9324, 1935.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1899, the local postage stamps were overprinted "Guam" as was done for the other former Spanish colonies, but this was discontinued shortly thereafter and regular U.S. postage stamps have been used ever since. Because Guam is also part of the U.S. Postal System (\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_abbreviations" title="List of U.S. state abbreviations">\n        postal abbreviation\n       </a>\n       : GU,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">\n        ZIP code range\n       </a>\n       : 96910\xe2\x80\x9396932), mail to Guam from the U.S. mainland is considered domestic and no additional charges are required. Private shipping companies, such as FedEx, UPS, and DHL, however, have no obligation to do so, and do not regard Guam as domestic.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The speed of mail traveling between Guam and the states varies depending on size and time of year. Light, first-class items generally take less than a week to or from the mainland, but larger first-class or Priority items can take a week or two. Fourth-class mail, such as magazines, are transported by sea after reaching Hawaii. Most residents use post office boxes or private mail boxes, although residential delivery is becoming increasingly available. Incoming mail not from the Americas should be addressed to "Guam" instead of "USA" to avoid being routed the long way through the U.S. mainland and possibly charged a higher rate (especially from Asia).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Commercial Port of Guam is the island\'s lifeline because most products must be shipped into Guam for consumers. It receives the weekly calls of the Hawaii-based shipping line\n       <a href="/wiki/Matson,_Inc." title="Matson, Inc.">\n        Matson, Inc.\n       </a>\n       whose container ships connect Guam with Honolulu, Hawaii, Los Angeles, California, Oakland, California and Seattle, Washington. The port is also the regional transhipment hub for over 500,000 customers throughout the Micronesian region. The port is the shipping and receiving point for containers designated for the island\'s U.S. Department of Defense installations, Andersen Air Force Base and Commander, Naval Forces Marianas and eventually the Third Marine Expeditionary Force.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guam is served by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_B._Won_Pat_International_Airport" title="Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport">\n        Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport\n       </a>\n       , which is a hub for\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">\n        United Airlines\n       </a>\n       . The island is outside the United States customs zone so Guam is responsible for establishing and operating its own customs and quarantine agency and jurisdiction. Therefore, the\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">\n        U.S. Customs and Border Protection\n       </a>\n       only carries immigration (but not customs) functions. Since Guam is under federal immigration jurisdiction, passengers arriving directly from the United States skip immigration and proceed directly to Guam Customs and Quarantine.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, due to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visa_waiver_program#Guam_and_Northern_Mariana_Islands_Visa_Waiver_Program" title="Visa waiver program">\n        Guam and CNMI visa waiver program\n       </a>\n       for certain countries, an eligibility pre-clearance check is carried on Guam for flights to the States. For travel from the Northern Mariana Islands to Guam, a pre-flight passport and visa check is performed before boarding the flight to Guam. On flights from Guam to the Northern Mariana Islands, no immigration check is performed. Traveling between Guam and the States through a foreign point, however, does require a passport.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most residents travel within Guam using personally owned vehicles. The local government currently outsources the only public bus system (\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="Guam Regional Transit Authority">\n        Guam Regional Transit Authority\n       </a>\n       ), and some commercial companies operate buses between tourist-frequented locations\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">\n        Ecology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ecology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Brown_tree_snake">\n        Brown tree snake\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Brown tree snake">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="416" data-file-width="640" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg/220px-Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg/330px-Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg/440px-Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brown_tree_snake_Boiga_irregularis_USGS_Photograph.sized.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Brown_tree_snake" title="Brown tree snake">\n          Brown tree snake\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Believed to be a\n       <a href="/wiki/Stowaway" title="Stowaway">\n        stowaway\n       </a>\n       on a U.S. military transport near the end of World War II, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Brown_tree_snake" title="Brown tree snake">\n        brown tree snake\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Boiga irregularis\n       </i>\n       ) was accidentally introduced to Guam, which previously had no native species of snake. It nearly eliminated the native bird population. The problem was exacerbated because the snake has no natural predators on the island. The brown tree snake, known locally as the\n       <i>\n        kulebla\n       </i>\n       , is native to northern and eastern coasts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">\n        Papua New Guinea\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">\n        Solomon Islands\n       </a>\n       . It is slightly venomous, but relatively harmless to human beings; it is nocturnal. Although some studies have suggested a high density of these serpents on Guam, residents rarely see them. The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">\n        United States Department of Agriculture\n       </a>\n       has trained detector dogs to keep the snakes out of the island\'s cargo flow. The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">\n        United States Geological Survey\n       </a>\n       also has dogs that can detect snakes in forested environments around the region\'s islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Before the introduction of the brown tree snake, Guam was home to several endemic bird species. Among them were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_rail" title="Guam rail">\n        Guam rail\n       </a>\n       (or\n       <i>\n        ko\'ko\'\n       </i>\n       bird in Chamorro) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_flycatcher" title="Guam flycatcher">\n        Guam flycatcher\n       </a>\n       , both common throughout the island. Today the flycatcher is entirely extinct and the Guam rail is extinct in the wild but bred in captivity by the Division of Aquatic and Wildlife Resources. The devastation caused by the snake has been significant over the past several decades. As many as twelve bird species are believed to have been driven to extinction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarzluffAngell2007_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MarzluffAngell2007-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to many elders, ko\'ko\' birds were common in Guam before World War II.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other bird species threatened by the brown tree snake include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_crow" title="Mariana crow">\n        Mariana crow\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_swiftlet" title="Mariana swiftlet">\n        Mariana swiftlet\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Micronesian_starling" title="Micronesian starling">\n        Micronesian starling\n       </a>\n       , though populations are present on other islands, including Rota.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarzluffAngell2007_53-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MarzluffAngell2007-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guam is said to have many more insects and 40 times more spiders than neighboring islands, because their natural predators birds are severely diminished, and the forests are almost completely silent due to lack of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birdsong" title="Birdsong">\n        birdsong\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="external autonumber" href="http://news.rice.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/0914_SPIDER-b2-big.jpg" rel="nofollow">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n        <a class="external autonumber" href="http://news.rice.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/0914_SPIDER4-webs-big.jpg" rel="nofollow">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n        Forest on Guam swathed in spider webs.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coconut_rhinoceros_beetle">\n        Coconut rhinoceros beetle\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Coconut rhinoceros beetle">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg/220px-Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg/330px-Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg/440px-Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oryctes_nasicornis_Thailand.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oryctes_rhinoceros" title="Oryctes rhinoceros">\n          Coconut rhinoceros beetle\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       An infestation of the coconut rhinoceros beetle (CRB),\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oryctes_rhinoceros" title="Oryctes rhinoceros">\n         Oryctes rhinoceros\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , was detected on Guam on September 12, 2007. CRB is not known to occur in the United States except in\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">\n        American Samoa\n       </a>\n       . Delimiting surveys performed September 13\xe2\x80\x9325, 2007, indicated that the infestation was limited to Tumon Bay and Faifai Beach, an area of approximately 900 acres (3.6\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). Guam Department of Agriculture (GDA) placed quarantine on all properties within the Tumon area on October 5 and later expanded the quarantine to about 2,500 acres (10\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) on October 25; approximately 0.5 miles (800\xc2\xa0m) radius in all directions from all known locations of CRB infestation. CRB is native to Southern Asia and distributed throughout Asia and the Western Pacific including\n       <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">\n        Sri Lanka\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">\n        Upolu\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">\n        Samoa\n       </a>\n       , American Samoa,\n       <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">\n        Palau\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Britain" title="New Britain">\n        New Britain\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Papua_(region)" title="West Papua (region)">\n        West Irian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Ireland_(island)" title="New Ireland (island)">\n        New Ireland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Manus_Island" title="Manus Island">\n        Pak Island and Manus Island\n       </a>\n       (New Guinea),\n       <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">\n        Fiji\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cocos_(Keeling)_Islands" title="Cocos (Keeling) Islands">\n        Cocos (Keeling) Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">\n        Mauritius\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R\xc3\xa9union">\n        Reunion\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_invasive_animal_species">\n        Other invasive animal species\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Other invasive animal species">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011_Feb,_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan,_10.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1196" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg/170px-2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg/255px-2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg/340px-2011_Feb%2C_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan%2C_10.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011_Feb,_Puerto_Princesa_to_Nasiduan,_10.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Adult female\n         <a href="/wiki/Carabao" title="Carabao">\n          carabao\n         </a>\n         and calf\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       From the seventeenth through nineteenth centuries, the Spanish introduced pigs, dogs, chickens, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_deer" title="Philippine deer">\n        Philippine deer\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Rusa mariannus\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Black_francolin" title="Black francolin">\n        black francolins\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Carabao" title="Carabao">\n        carabao\n       </a>\n       (a subspecies of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_buffalo" title="Domestic buffalo">\n        water buffalo\n       </a>\n       ), which have cultural significance. Herds of carabao obstruct military base operations and harm native ecosystems. After birth control and adoption efforts were ineffective, the U.S. military began culling the herds in 2002 leading to organized protests from island residents.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other introduced species include\n       <a href="/wiki/Cane_toad" title="Cane toad">\n        cane toads\n       </a>\n       imported in 1937, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Achatina_achatina" title="Achatina achatina">\n        giant African snail\n       </a>\n       (an agricultural pest introduced during World War\xc2\xa0II by Japanese occupation troops) and more recently frog species which could threaten crops in addition to providing additional food for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Brown_tree_snake" title="Brown tree snake">\n        brown tree snake\n       </a>\n       population. Reports of loud chirping frogs native to Puerto Rico and known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_coqu%C3%AD" title="Common coqu\xc3\xad">\n        coqu\xc3\xad\n       </a>\n       , that may have arrived from Hawaii, have led to fears that the noise could threaten Guam\'s tourism.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Guam has no native amphibian species, but now a total of eight amphibian species has been established in Guam.\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Litoria_fallax" title="Litoria fallax">\n         Litoria fallax\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (native to the eastern coast of Australia) has been present in Guam since 1968, and\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhinella_marina" title="Rhinella marina">\n         Rhinella marina\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (the cane toad) was brought to the island in 1937. The other 6 amphibian species, namely\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hylarana_guentheri" title="Hylarana guentheri">\n         Hylarana guentheri\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (native to mainland Asia),\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Microhyla_pulchra" title="Microhyla pulchra">\n         Microhyla pulchra\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (native to mainland Asia),\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Polypedates_braueri" title="Polypedates braueri">\n         Polypedates braueri\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (endemic to Taiwan),\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleutherodactylus_planirostris" title="Eleutherodactylus planirostris">\n         Eleutherodactylus planirostris\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (native to the Caribbean),\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fejervarya_cancrivora" title="Fejervarya cancrivora">\n         Fejervarya cancrivora\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (the Guam variety being most closely related to\n       <i>\n        F. cancrivora\n       </i>\n       found in Taiwan), and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fejervarya_limnocharis" title="Fejervarya limnocharis">\n         Fejervarya limnocharis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (native to Southeast Asia), have been in Guam since 2003.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many species were likely inadvertently introduced via shipping cargo, especially from Taiwan, mainland China, and Southeast Asia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Introduced feral pigs and deer, over-hunting, and habitat loss from human development are also major factors in the decline and loss of Guam\'s native plants and animals.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Threats_to_indigenous_plants">\n        Threats to indigenous plants\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Threats to indigenous plants">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Invading animal species are not the only threat to Guam\'s native flora. Tinangaja, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant_virus" title="Plant virus">\n        virus\n       </a>\n       affecting coconut palms, was first observed on the island in 1917 when\n       <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">\n        copra\n       </a>\n       production was still a major part of Guam\'s economy. Though coconut plantations no longer exist on the island, the dead and infected trees that have resulted from the epidemic are seen throughout the forests of Guam.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the past century, the dense forests of northern Guam have been largely replaced by thick\n       <i>\n        tangan-tangan\n       </i>\n       brush (\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Leucaena_leucocephala" title="Leucaena leucocephala">\n         Leucaena leucocephala\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ). Much of Guam\'s foliage was lost during\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       . In 1947, the U.S. military is thought to have planted tangan-tangan by seeding the island from the air to prevent\n       <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">\n        erosion\n       </a>\n       . Tangan-tangan was present on the island before 1905.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In southern Guam, non-native grass species dominate much of the landscape. Although the colorful and impressive flame tree (\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Delonix_regia" title="Delonix regia">\n         Delonix regia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ) is found throughout the Marianas, the tree on Guam has been largely decimated.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wildfires">\n        Wildfires\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Wildfires">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guam_Grassland.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="150" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6f/Guam_Grassland.jpg" width="150"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guam_Grassland.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Guam\'s grassland\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">\n        Wildfires\n       </a>\n       plague the forested areas of Guam every\n       <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">\n        dry season\n       </a>\n       despite the island\'s humid climate. Most fires are caused by humans with 80% resulting from arson.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Poachers often start fires to attract deer to the new growth. Invasive grass species that rely on fire as part of their natural life cycle grow in many regularly burned areas. Grasslands and "barrens" have replaced previously forested areas leading to greater soil erosion. During the rainy season, sediment is carried by the heavy rains into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fena_Lake" title="Fena Lake">\n        Fena Lake\n       </a>\n       Reservoir and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ugum_River" title="Ugum River">\n        Ugum River\n       </a>\n       , leading to water quality problems for southern Guam. Eroded silt also destroys the marine life in reefs around the island. Soil stabilization efforts by volunteers and forestry workers (planting trees) have had little success in preserving natural habitats.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Aquatic_preserves">\n        Aquatic preserves\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Aquatic preserves">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tumon_Beach.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1197" data-file-width="1708" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Tumon_Beach.JPG/220px-Tumon_Beach.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Tumon_Beach.JPG/330px-Tumon_Beach.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Tumon_Beach.JPG/440px-Tumon_Beach.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tumon_Beach.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Having previously experienced extensive\n         <a href="/wiki/Dredging" title="Dredging">\n          dredging\n         </a>\n         , Tumon Bay is now a marine wildlife preserve.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Efforts have been made to protect Guam\'s coral reef habitats from pollution, eroded silt and overfishing, problems that have led to decreased fish populations. (Since Guam is a significant vacation spot for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scuba_diver" title="Scuba diver">\n        scuba divers\n       </a>\n       , this is important.) In recent years, the Department of Agriculture, Division of Aquatic and Wildlife Resources has established several new marine preserves where fish populations are monitored by biologists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Before adopting\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">\n        U.S. Environmental Protection Agency\n       </a>\n       standards, portions of Tumon Bay were dredged by the hotel chains to provide a better experience for hotel guests.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tumon Bay has since been made into a preserve. A federal\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Guam National Wildlife Refuge">\n        Guam National Wildlife Refuge\n       </a>\n       in northern Guam protects the decimated\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_turtle" title="Sea turtle">\n        sea turtle\n       </a>\n       population in addition to a small colony of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mariana_fruit_bats" title="Mariana fruit bats">\n        Mariana fruit bats\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Harvest of sea turtle eggs was a common occurrence on Guam before World War II. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Green_sea_turtle" title="Green sea turtle">\n        green sea turtle\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Chelonia mydas\n       </i>\n       ) was harvested legally on Guam before August 1978, when it was listed as threatened under the Endangered Species Act. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_sea_turtle" title="Hawksbill sea turtle">\n        hawksbill sea turtle\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Eretmochelys imbricata\n       </i>\n       ) has been on the endangered list since 1970. In an effort to ensure protection of sea turtles on Guam, routine sightings are counted during aerial surveys and nest sites are recorded and monitored for hatchlings.\n      </p>\n      <center>\n       <table class="wikitable">\n        <tr>\n         <td>\n          <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 789px;_width: 789px;">\n           <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 255px">\n            <div style="width: 255px">\n             <div class="thumb" style="width: 250px;">\n              <div style="margin:15px auto;">\n               <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Whitespotted_boxfish_Ostracion_meleagris_photo_Randall_J_E.jpg">\n                <img alt="" data-file-height="158" data-file-width="211" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Whitespotted_boxfish_Ostracion_meleagris_photo_Randall_J_E.jpg" width="220"/>\n               </a>\n              </div>\n             </div>\n             <div class="gallerytext">\n              <p>\n               <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whitespotted_boxfish" title="Whitespotted boxfish">\n                Whitespotted boxfish\n               </a>\n               (\n               <i>\n                <a href="/wiki/Ostracion_meleagris" title="Ostracion meleagris">\n                 Ostracion meleagris\n                </a>\n               </i>\n               )\n              </p>\n             </div>\n            </div>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n        <tr>\n         <th>\n          <center>\n           Reef fish of Guam\n          </center>\n         </th>\n        </tr>\n       </table>\n      </center>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">\n        Colleges and universities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG/220px-University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG/330px-University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG/440px-University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Guam_Campus.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The central campus at the\n         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Guam" title="University of Guam">\n          University of Guam\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Guam" title="University of Guam">\n        University of Guam\n       </a>\n       (UOG) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Community_College" title="Guam Community College">\n        Guam Community College\n       </a>\n       , both fully accredited by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="Western Association of Schools and Colleges">\n        Western Association of Schools and Colleges\n       </a>\n       , offer courses in higher education.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       UOG is a member of the exclusive group of only 76\n       <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">\n        land-grant institutions\n       </a>\n       in the entire United States.\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_University" title="Pacific Islands University">\n        Pacific Islands University\n       </a>\n       is a small Christian liberal arts institution nationally accredited by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Transnational_Association_of_Christian_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Transnational Association of Christian Colleges and Schools">\n        Transnational Association of Christian Colleges and Schools\n       </a>\n       . They offer courses at both the undergraduate and graduate levels.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_schools">\n        Primary and secondary schools\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary schools">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Guam" title="List of schools in Guam">\n        List of schools in Guam\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Department_of_Education" title="Guam Department of Education">\n        Guam Department of Education\n       </a>\n       serves the entire island of Guam. In 2000, 32,000 students attended Guam\'s public schools. Guam Public Schools have struggled with problems such as high dropout rates and poor test scores.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merrow_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Merrow-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-State-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Guam\'s educational system has always faced unique challenges as a small community located 6,000 miles (9,700\xc2\xa0km) from the U.S. mainland with a very diverse student body including many students who come from backgrounds without traditional American education.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peabody_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Peabody-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An economic downturn in Guam since the mid-1990s has compounded the problems in schools.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guam_Legislature_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Guam_Legislature-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Before September 1997, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Defense" title="U.S. Department of Defense">\n        U.S. Department of Defense\n       </a>\n       partnered with Guam Board of Education.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In September 1997, the DoDEA opened its own schools for children of military personnel.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Defense_Education_Activity" title="Department of Defense Education Activity">\n        DoDEA\n       </a>\n       schools, which also serve children of some federal civilian employees, had an attendance of 2,500 in 2000. DoDEA Guam operates three elementary/middle schools and one high school.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DODEA_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DODEA-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries">\n        Public libraries\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Public libraries">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Public_Library_System" title="Guam Public Library System">\n        Guam Public Library System\n       </a>\n       operates the Nieves M. Flores Memorial Library in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hag%C3%A5t%C3%B1a" title="Hag\xc3\xa5t\xc3\xb1a">\n        Hag\xc3\xa5t\xc3\xb1a\n       </a>\n       and five branch libraries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">\n        Health care\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Health care">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The Government of Guam maintains the island\'s main health care facility,\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam_Memorial_Hospital" title="Guam Memorial Hospital">\n        Guam Memorial Hospital\n       </a>\n       , in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamuning,_Guam" title="Tamuning, Guam">\n        Tamuning\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       U.S. board certified doctors and dentists practice in all specialties. In addition, the U.S. Naval Hospital in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agana_Heights,_Guam" title="Agana Heights, Guam">\n        Agana Heights\n       </a>\n       serves active-duty members and dependents of the military community.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There is one subscriber-based\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_ambulance" title="Air ambulance">\n        air ambulance\n       </a>\n       located on the island, CareJet, which provides emergency patient transportation across Guam and surrounding islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A private hospital, the\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guam_Regional_Medical_City&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guam Regional Medical City (page does not exist)">\n        Guam Regional Medical City\n       </a>\n       opened its doors in early 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRMC_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GRMC-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Film-making">\n        Film-making\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Film-making">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Over the years, a number of films have been shot on Guam, including\n       <i>\n        Shiro\'s Head\n       </i>\n       (directed by the Muna brothers) and the government-funded\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Max_Havoc:_Curse_of_the_Dragon" title="Max Havoc: Curse of the Dragon">\n         Max Havoc: Curse of the Dragon\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (2004). Although set on Guam,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/No_Man_Is_an_Island_(film)" title="No Man Is an Island (film)">\n         No Man Is an Island\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (1962) was not shot there, but in the Republic of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n
